First of all, you have to understand that Jermaine Franklin had no business in the same ring as him.  You would have thought of Joshua, like a ballet dancer,   boxed on tiptoe. Small jumps in moderate time, somersaults, down to earth, without allegro.  I have nothing against Jermaine Franklin. He couldn't do better. His record remains intact for never having been knocked out in his career.  Remember, Joshua was a 12-1 favorite to take the win. He had promised to retire from boxing if he lost. Sure, he didn't lose, but his victory didn't make him more famous.  All told, Joshua will add nearly fifteen million (US) to his fortune of over $113 million pounds.  Not bad for a 36 minutes of work under TV reflectors.  And now,  that he has found his way to victory, he allows himself to challenge the WBC champion, Tyson Fury. If Fury ever accepts, Joshua will be wobbled, or if you like better: He will be beaten to the hilt if he doesn't  looking after himself.  How to explain that a pugilist who swept away everything in his path as an amateur to finally win the gold medal at the London Olympics in 2012, and then become world champion among the pros, can he become so amorphous in a fight? Admittedly, Joshua had every chance of getting the knockout to his rival.  Why didn't he? Where is this ferocity that we once knew about him?  After all, he has 22 knockout wins during his career, but no knockouts in his last five outings. For what?  Out of pity? Out of recklessness? By incapacity? For lack of will? For lack of heartâ€¦? I don't know  It's true that he competed against Oleksandr Usyk on two occasions, but he could have handed the courtesy to Andy Ruiz and finished Jermaine Franklin, but no, he decided to tap dance.  What I do know is that it's better to listen to the advice of Barry Hearn from Matchroom Boxing and not accept  stooges, but second-class pugilists.  Currently, following this performance against Franklin, it is obvious that he would not last long against a Tyson Fury, an Oleksandr Usyk, or a Deontay Wilder, or a Joe Joyce. No, I would see him against a Daniel Dubois, Frank Sanchez, Zheillei Zhang, Trevor Bryan and Arslanbek Makhmudov.  His young audience is calling for him, unlike the older ones who would like to see him face Dillian Whyte again, whom he has already defeated by technical K.-O.  in the seventh round in 2015. Whyte is now 35 years old and he is boxing simply in the hope of increasing his retirement pension.

AJ's recent performances in the ring have shown hesitancy and conservatism, which may stem from the deep hurt he suffered from defeats by Ruiz and Usyk. Subconsciously, he may fear being knocked down or facing another defeat. While his latest fight was solid, it lacked the boldness and aggression of his previous bouts. However, one positive takeaway from the fight was his resilience and strong chin, as he absorbed several powerful shots without showing any visible effects. Nonetheless, as he ages, it's important to remember that his glory days may have come and gone, a realization that is ironic given his past match against Klitch. Time flies by quickly, and AJ must now find a way to rebuild his confidence and adapt to the changes that come with age.

The former 2-time world heavyweight champion Anthony Joshua looked a bit nervous for several rounds, like he was so insecure about his own weapons in the ring.  Can be said somewhat understandably considering the pressure he wears on his shoulders after his two straight defeats to the skilled champion Oleksandr Usyk. While opinions may differ, I thought it was overall a weaker performance by Joshua as he looked very hesitant at times. He could have went for the KO but played it safe and realued on winning a decision contest. I believe his confidence is low and he really could have used a knock-out victory over Jermain Franklin as a booster.  A.J seems to have regressed a bit and is now more â€œOne Dimensionalâ€ than ever. Ever since his loss to Andy Ruiz Jr. back in 2019 he have been hesitant to let his hands go more often and seems hesitant to engage. Also I believe Usyk really did a mental number on him and that further have made Joshua regressed.  All that muscle mass Joshua have, all that power - yet so little ring aggression.  There is only one way to change this negative development for Joshua and that is simpley FIGHT ON. Joshua needs to book himself to be buissy in the ring with several more fights where he can regain his confidence in his abilities and build himself up. There is no other way for him. Joshua must stop being so selective in the ring and become more dedicated to his craft by fighting more often. 1-2 fights per year don't cut it.  He needs a year with 5 fights where he is buissy against varied styles against decent enough opposition in different locations. That would be the ticket to fix him. The rest would be up to himself and taking care of his mentality.
